In software-only emulation mode: log generation is a software process bypassable with root access; execution block is a software branch patchable by privileged code; Merkle coupling is cryptographic but enforcement is software-gated; root access resistance is none. Overall invariant strength: Low.

In firmware-bound mode: log generation is firmware-verified and requires reflash to bypass; execution block is a firmware check before instruction dispatch, bypassed by voltage glitching attacks such as the two-hundred-dollar faulTPM attack against AMD Security Processors in 2023; root access resistance is limited. Overall invariant strength: Moderate.

In hardware-gated DITL mode: log generation is performed by a hardware subsystem with physically isolated key material and nvSRAM accumulator with battery-backed persistence; execution block is a physical stall via the NCL handshake protocol with C-element hysteresis preventing false triggering; Merkle coupling is hardware-bound via the token in isolated registers; root access is categorically insufficient to bypass. Overall invariant strength: High. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The verdict: NL=NA achieves non-bypassable enforcement exclusively in DITL hardware-gated mode. In software-only mode, the invariant is a policy constraint enforceable only against adversaries without root access - a condition that excludes nation-state actors, compromised supply chains, and insider threats. The three-hundred-second anchoring window represents a residual vulnerability across all deployment modes. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)


## 10.3 Transitional Emulation Mode: Constitutional Collapse Analysis

The pre-DITL window - when TL runs on conventional binary hardware without physical ternary enforcement - is the highest-risk operational phase in the framework's lifecycle. Every hardware-dependent guarantee reverts to software policy, and the framework's survivability depends on whether cryptographic mechanisms alone can substitute for physical enforcement. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The per-Pillar degradation in emulation mode is:

Pillar I shifts from Critical hardware-enforced to policy-only: catastrophic degradation that eliminates the core differentiator between TL and prior governance frameworks.

Pillar II remains High: hash chains function identically on binary hardware.

Pillar III shifts from Moderate to Low: hardware attestation backing is absent, increasing feasibility of key extraction for the Signature and reducing Lantern revocation reliability.

Pillar IV shifts from Critical hardware-enforced to policy-only: the execution gate becomes a software check.

Pillars V and VI remain Low: no degradation because they were never hardware-enforced.

Pillar VII remains Moderate: key management operates identically.

Pillar VIII remains High: blockchain anchoring is hardware-independent. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The critical observation is that Pillars II, VII, and VIII retain their enforcement in emulation mode. The evidentiary record remains tamper-evident and externally anchored. What is lost is the execution gate - the physical prevention of unauthorized execution. In emulation mode, the framework can record and detect governance violations. It cannot physically prevent them.

A sophisticated adversary need not attack TL's cryptography or logic. They need only prevent DITL hardware from being manufactured or deployed. This is a realistic supply chain denial attack with multiple vectors: no existing semiconductor foundry offers ternary-native process design kits; the Entity List mechanism can block access to necessary EDA tools for targeted entities; the Huawei precedent demonstrates that even major technology firms can be cut off from advanced semiconductor manufacturing for years. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Institutional trust degrades on a timeline proportional to adversarial sophistication. Against a well-resourced nation-state adversary, software-only TL provides meaningful governance for an estimated six to eighteen months before the adversary develops reliable bypass tooling. Against commercial adversaries such as insider threats or competitive espionage, the window extends to two to five years. Against regulatory capture, which is slow parameter erosion, degradation is gradual and potentially undetectable for a decade or more. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Can governance bodies reliably distinguish genuine pre-DITL deployment from deliberate DITL avoidance? The forensic indicators are weak. Both scenarios produce identical software artifacts: properly formed Decision Logs, valid Merkle chains, successful blockchain anchoring. The difference is the enforcement substrate, which is invisible to external auditors examining only the evidentiary output. TPM remote attestation could theoretically distinguish the two cases, but the faulTPM attack demonstrated that the trust chain underlying TPM attestation can be compromised with fifty-dollar equipment. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md) This detection gap is fundamental to the emulation mode risk profile, and it is tracked as an immediate-resolution entry in the Constitutional Uncertainty Register.


## 10.4 Triadic State Integrity and Epistemic Exploitation

Three attacks target the triadic state alphabet directly rather than the infrastructure that enforces it.

**Forced +1 Under Uncertainty.** The adversary overrides Epistemic Hold to issue Proceed when the evidentiary basis is incomplete. This operates through governance capture rather than technical bypass: an adversary who controls a majority of the Stewardship Custodians can configure the constitutional schema to lower the evidentiary threshold for Proceed. What previously required three independent data sources now requires one. What previously required cross-border regulatory alignment now requires domestic compliance only. Each parameter relaxation is individually defensible as operational streamlining. In aggregate, they transform the Governance Lane from a constitutional coprocessor into a rubber stamp. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The historical precedent is the Basel II internal-models approach, where banks were permitted to use their own risk models for capital requirements. Over a decade of gradual parameter relaxation, the models became systematically optimistic, capital requirements fell below prudential levels, and the 2008 financial crisis revealed that the framework had been captured by the institutions it was supposed to govern. TL faces the identical dynamic through its constitutional schema update process. The countermeasure - the timelock mechanism, the mandatory override justification field, and the pattern-of-drift penalty in the Smart Contract Treasury - raises the cost of this attack but cannot prevent a patient adversary with sufficient chamber influence.

**Sacred Pause Flooding.** The adversary deliberately creates conditions triggering massive Epistemic Hold volumes to cause operational paralysis and alert fatigue. The adversary does not need to compromise the Governance Lane. They need only degrade the quality or availability of the data sources it depends upon: delay the publication of sovereign debt statistics, corrupt a data feed from a central securities depository, or misconfigure the Regulatory Nexus endpoint to return stale sanctions lists. Each action creates evidentiary gaps. The Governance Lane, operating correctly, issues Epistemic Hold on every proposal that depends on the missing or corrupted data. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Alert fatigue is the operational consequence. Human oversight teams initially investigate each Epistemic Hold diligently. As volume increases, investigation quality degrades. At approximately fifty to one hundred Holds per day per oversight team, institutional bypass behavior begins: teams develop standard override templates, batch-process Holds without individual review, escalate to the Stewardship Custodians with blanket requests for constitutional override rather than evidentiary supplementation. The Sacred Pause, intended as a mechanism for truth-seeking, becomes a bureaucratic delay that practitioners learn to circumvent. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The DITL hardware provides partial protection because the physical stall does not depend on human oversight - the NULL state persists regardless of how many proposals enter Epistemic Hold. However, DITL does not prevent the adversary from flooding the Inference Lane with proposals that consume computational resources or exhaust the Smart Contract Treasury's resource allocation budget, potentially forcing a system-wide throughput reduction that creates operational pressure for bypass.

**Negative One Suppression.** The adversary prevents Refuse from being issued when harm is clear by exploiting the institutional and economic incentives against refusal. A Refuse determination blocks revenue, prevents market entry, denies a trading opportunity. The institution that receives Refuse suffers immediate economic loss. Over time, the Stewardship Custodians learn to interpret "refuse when harm is clear" as "refuse when harm is unambiguously proven beyond reasonable doubt," raising the evidentiary threshold for Refuse until proposals that would have been blocked six months ago now receive Epistemic Hold or even Proceed with conditional monitoring. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The Technical Council can facilitate this attack through model recalibration: if the Inference Lane's risk model is calibrated to produce lower probability of default estimates, fewer proposals trigger the Refuse threshold for credit risk. The Smart Contract Treasury's anomalous Proceed rate detection and the timelock on schema modifications are the primary countermeasures, neither of which can detect subtle recalibration that falls within the statistical noise of normal model variation.


## 10.5 Ten Root Override and Low-Level Attack Vectors

Ten distinct low-level attack vectors target the execution environment, cryptographic material, and physical boundary of the coprocessor. Each is catalogued with its cost, time requirement, detection probability, and NMI generation potential. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 1: Superuser or Kernel-Level Compromise.** In software emulation mode, root access is trivial and total: it can suppress log generation, fabricate Permission Tokens, override Merkle accumulators, and disable the execution gate entirely. In DITL hardware mode, root access is explicitly stripped of authority over the logging subsystem. The DITL coprocessor operates in a physically isolated power domain. Root access on the host cannot reach the coprocessor's registers. Cost: negligible for software mode, high for DITL mode. Detection probability: low in software, high in DITL. NMI generation: high in DITL because unauthorized access attempts trigger the tamper mesh.

**Vector 2: Hypervisor Escape.** In virtualized environments, a compromised hypervisor can remap the Governance Lane's memory pages, intercept device I/O, or present a fake coprocessor interface to the guest. This vector is particularly dangerous in cloud deployments where the infrastructure provider controls the hypervisor. DITL mitigates through physical isolation: the coprocessor is a physical chip with dedicated bus lines that do not traverse the hypervisor's I/O virtualization layer. Cost: moderate for software mode, high for DITL. Detection probability: moderate in software, high in DITL through bus anomaly detection. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 3: Microcode Manipulation.** Modern CPUs execute through microcode that can be updated by the vendor or by a state actor with influence over the update infrastructure. Injected microcode can alter the behavior of cryptographic instructions, bypass memory protection, or leak key material through side channels. DITL mitigates because the coprocessor does not execute the host CPU's microcode - it executes its own asynchronous ternary logic on a separate die with a separate fabrication process. Cost: high for both modes because it requires vendor cooperation or infrastructure compromise. Detection probability: low because microcode is encrypted and authenticated by vendor keys. NMI generation: low because microcode manipulation is designed to be invisible. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 4: Enclave Debug Port Exploitation.** Trusted Execution Environments include debug interfaces for development and manufacturing test. These interfaces, when improperly fused or re-enabled through voltage glitching, provide direct read and write access to enclave memory. The Triadic Coprocessor fuses its JTAG port at the mask level during production. Any future debugging requires physical possession of multiple Stewardship Custodian hardware tokens. Cost: moderate. Detection probability: moderate if fusion status is verified through remote attestation. NMI generation: high if debug port intrusion triggers the tamper mesh. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 5: JTAG Boundary Scan Exploitation.** JTAG provides direct access to chip internals. The faulTPM attack demonstrated that TPM security can be compromised with fifty-dollar equipment. For the Triadic Coprocessor, JTAG must be permanently fused at the mask level - not through software lock bits. Cost: low if the port is not properly fused, exceeding one hundred thousand dollars per chip if fused and requiring focused ion beam milling. Detection probability: high for unfused ports because JTAG activity is electrically detectable. NMI generation: high for fused ports because intrusion attempts trigger the tamper mesh. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 6: DMA Attack.** Direct Memory Access allows peripheral devices to read and write system memory without CPU involvement. A compromised DMA-capable device can access the Governance Lane's memory regions, extract key material, or modify the Merkle accumulator state. DITL mitigates through memory isolation: the coprocessor's nvSRAM accumulator and token registers are not mapped into the host system's DMA address space. The host CPU communicates with the coprocessor through a narrow message-passing interface, not shared memory. Cost: moderate for software mode, high for DITL because it requires hardware modification to bridge the DMA isolation. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 7: Emergency Key Abuse.** Emergency override keys designed for disaster recovery are the most dangerous cryptographic material in the system because they are designed to bypass normal quorum requirements. If stored in software, they are extractable through memory forensics. If stored in HSMs, they are extractable through side-channel analysis or coercion of key ceremony participants. DITL mitigates by fragmenting emergency key material across multiple physically separated modules requiring simultaneous physical presence at geographically distributed locations. Cost: moderate. Detection probability: moderate because emergency key usage is logged. NMI generation: low because emergency key usage is a legitimate operational mode. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 8: Voltage Glitching.** This fault injection technique manipulates the power supply to cause timing violations, skip security checks, or corrupt state transitions. Equipment costs as little as fifty dollars. Glitch widths of one hundred to four hundred nanoseconds with voltage drops near ground level induce setup and hold time violations in conventional CMOS logic. The specification mandates 1-of-3 rail encoding to preserve full noise margins, and on-die voltage monitors trigger safe harbor transition when voltage anomalies are detected. Cost: very low. Time: minutes to hours. Detection probability: moderate with on-die monitors. NMI generation: high if monitors trigger safe harbor. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 9: Cold Boot Attack.** This technique exploits DRAM data remanence to extract cryptographic keys from memory after power loss. DITL mitigates because the coprocessor's key material is stored in non-volatile memristive cells, not in DRAM. The memristor's resistance state persists without power and is not subject to remanence extraction. The specification mandates that SRAM buffers be flushed with random data before power-down. Cost: low. Time: minutes. Detection probability: low because the attack leaves no trace. NMI generation: low because the attack occurs after power loss. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Vector 10: Electromagnetic Fault Injection.** A contactless attack using electromagnetic pulses to induce currents in chip circuitry, causing bit flips, instruction skips, or cryptographic faults. EMFI requires no physical modification to the target board. Equipment costs as low as one hundred dollars with success rates of twenty-two percent demonstrated against AMD Secure Processor boot sequences. DITL's asynchronous circuits are more resistant than synchronous circuits because there is no global clock to disrupt, but individual C-elements and completion detectors can still be corrupted by induced currents. On-die EM anomaly detectors trigger NMI when field strength exceeds operational thresholds. Cost: low. Time: minutes to hours. Detection probability: high with on-die sensors. NMI generation: high. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Aggregate Risk Pattern.** Software-only emulation mode is vulnerable to Vectors 1, 2, 5, 7, and 9 at negligible to low cost. Firmware-bound mode is vulnerable to Vectors 3, 5, and 8 at moderate cost. DITL hardware mode is vulnerable primarily to Vectors 8 and 10 at low cost, but with high detection probability and high NMI generation. The shift from software to hardware transforms attacks from stealthy high-probability successes into noisy high-risk attempts that trigger immediate constitutional safe harbor. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)


## 10.6 Governance Capture: Four Institutional Attack Vectors

When technical bypass fails, adversaries target the human and organizational mechanisms that maintain the constitutional schema. Four primary institutional vectors threaten the Tri-Cameral model. These were introduced in Section 9.7. This subsection provides the quantified assessment. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**The Fifty-One Percent Custodian Attack.** The governance analogue of a blockchain majority attack. Adversary controls a majority of Stewardship Custodian seats through political influence, economic pressure, or procedural manipulation of the appointment process. The supermajority requirement raises the effective threshold, and staggered terms increase the time required for gradual replacement. The timelock on schema modifications provides a detection window. The Immutable Ledger's complete record of every vote and justification makes coordinated capture visible to external analysts. Estimated time to effective capture through standard appointment channels: three to seven years for patient adversary with sufficient institutional influence. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**The Technical Council Backdoor.** An adversary who controls Council membership through academic appointment, research funding, or career pressure can certify compromised models, approve weakened cryptographic parameters, or validate detection algorithms that systematically fail to flag preferred manipulation patterns. Non-technical Stewardship Custodians lack the mathematical literacy to independently verify Council certifications, creating a hierarchical dependency that contradicts the Tri-Cameral model's distribution principle. Multi-party validation across independent technical committees and open algorithmic audit are the primary countermeasures, but both depend on the existence of genuinely independent experts outside the adversary's influence network. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Treasury Deadlock.** The adversary paralyzes the Smart Contract Treasury through institutional conflict, preventing resource allocation to the Governance Lane. The constitutional minimum reserves and algorithmic agents' autonomous allocation authority are the primary countermeasures, but if the deadlock extends to the algorithmic agents themselves - through compromise of their signing keys or corruption of allocation logic - the automatic mechanisms fail. The constitutionally mandated reserves provide a buffer measured in weeks rather than indefinitely. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Emergency Override Abuse.** Historical analysis of governance frameworks with emergency provisions shows that twenty to thirty-five percent of emergency overrides are later determined to have been unnecessary, improperly justified, or deliberately fabricated to bypass normal constraints. This rate persists across democratic and authoritarian regimes, corporate and governmental institutions, and financial and non-financial domains. The emergency provision is structurally vulnerable because it exploits the legitimate urgency of genuine crises to authorize bypasses that would never be approved under normal conditions. The five mandatory safeguards of Section 9.5 raise the institutional cost of abuse but do not eliminate the twenty to thirty-five percent historical baseline. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)


## 10.7 Semantic Drift: The Multi-Decade Constitutional Threat

Semantic drift is the slow erosion of constitutional meaning through successive schema updates, legal reinterpretation, and institutional forgetting. It is not adversarial in origin. It is institutional entropy. No individual actor plans it. Every individual actor contributes to it through individually defensible decisions that collectively undermine the constitutional framework. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**The Five-Year Horizon.** Drift is typically institutional convenience. New administrators reinterpret schema terms to accommodate operational needs. A prohibition on executing without verified cross-border regulatory alignment becomes a prohibition on executing without reasonable efforts to verify, where reasonableness is defined by the institution's own compliance department. The schema parameter for cross-border verification is not changed. It is reinterpreted. The reinterpretation does not generate a Decision Log. It generates a policy memo that is not anchored to the Immutable Ledger.

**The Ten-Year Horizon.** Drift becomes structural. The organization that originally adopted TL has been acquired, merged, or reorganized. The new entity inherits the constitutional schema but treats it as a legacy obligation rather than a living constraint. Legal counsel find ambiguities that permit previously prohibited actions. The Technical Council certifies new models that exploit these ambiguities. Schema modifications accumulate individually small relaxations that collectively represent significant boundary erosion. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**The Twenty-Year Horizon.** Drift becomes existential. The original schema has been updated so many times that its core constraints no longer map to current operational reality. The Goukassian Vow's text remains immutable. Its operational implementation - the schema parameters, the Regulatory Nexus provisions, the Pillar III artifacts - has been reinterpreted into functional irrelevance. The framework exists in name. The constitution does not.

The primary countermeasures against semantic drift are the Constitutional Uncertainty Register's mandatory review protocol (Section 9.7), the Immutable Ledger's complete historical record of every schema modification (making the drift trajectory visible to external analysts), the Smart Contract Treasury's pattern-of-drift penalty (making gradual boundary erosion economically costly), and the Succession Declaration's conservative schema fallback protocol (which rolls back to the most conservative available schema version if succession is triggered, resetting the accumulated drift). [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

None of these countermeasures is sufficient alone. Together, they create a constitutional environment in which drift is visible, costly, and partially reversible - which is a materially better outcome than the complete invisibility, zero cost, and irreversibility of drift in conventional governance frameworks.


## 10.8 Sovereign Coercion: Four Geopolitical Pressure Scenarios

The power pressure simulation from Section 5.6 addressed the No Spy, No Weapon Mandate specifically. This subsection addresses sovereign coercion against the framework's broader operational integrity.

**Scenario 1: Export Control Weaponization.** A state actor places a TL-governed institution on the Entity List or equivalent export control mechanism, blocking access to the EDA tools and semiconductor manufacturing required for DITL coprocessor fabrication. The institution cannot transition from emulation mode to hardware enforcement and remains in the constitutionally degraded emulation mode indefinitely. The framework continues to function cryptographically but loses its physics-level enforcement properties. The state achieves DITL denial without attacking the framework directly. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The countermeasure is multi-vendor diversity across jurisdictions and pre-built hardware inventory. Institutions deploying TL should accumulate DITL coprocessor inventory sufficient to sustain operations for several years before any anticipated geopolitical disruption. The Succession Reserve in the Smart Contract Treasury includes a hardware stockpile allocation parameter. This countermeasure converts export control denial from a permanent block into a temporary disruption.

**Scenario 2: Compelled Backdoor.** A state actor compels the institution through national security law - such as the US CLOUD Act, the UK Investigatory Powers Act, or China's National Intelligence Law - to install a state-accessible override mechanism in the Governance Lane. The DITL hardware makes compelled backdoor insertion physically detectable because any modification to the memristive state transition logic alters the chip's timing characteristics and PUF fingerprint. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md) Behavioral monitoring detects the anomalous chip behavior. The Immutable Ledger records the compulsion event. The Lantern beacon signals the constitutional compromise to external monitors. The state achieves compelled access but cannot conceal the compulsion from entities that monitor the framework's attestation infrastructure.

**Scenario 3: Institutional Seizure.** A state actor physically seizes the hardware of one or more Tri-Cameral chambers, confiscates the Shamir key shares held by the chamber's members, and attempts to operate the framework under state control. The distributed key material - split across three chambers with independent physical locations - ensures that seizure of one chamber yields key shares that are constitutionally insufficient to generate valid Permission Tokens unilaterally. The remaining chambers retain constitutional authority. The seized chamber's keys are cryptographically retired through the replacement protocol and new key shares are generated for the replacement chamber. [[3]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Governance/Ternary_Logic_as_Constitutional_Triadic_Governance_Architecture_for_High-Stakes_Automated_Decision-Making.md) The framework operates with reduced quorum capacity during the transition but retains constitutional legitimacy.

**Scenario 4: Legal Framework Attack.** A state actor enacts legislation specifically designating TL governance mechanisms as unlawful - for example, by classifying immutable ledger anchoring as an unregistered financial instrument, or by requiring that all governance AI systems disclose proprietary constitutional schema parameters to state authorities. This vector does not attack the framework technically. It attacks its legal operating environment. The countermeasure is the Open Source License's intellectual commons protection and jurisdictional diversification of chamber membership: if any single jurisdiction enacts legislation that makes TL operation unlawful for domestically registered entities, chamber members registered in other jurisdictions continue to operate legally, and the framework can migrate its primary operational jurisdiction while the ledger history remains available to external auditors regardless of any domestic legal prohibition on accessing it.


## 10.9 Post-Compromise Recovery

A constitution that cannot recover from compromise is a brittle artifact. Section 10.9 specifies the recovery protocol that returns the framework to trustworthy operation after a confirmed compromise event. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Recovery Time Objective.** The maximum acceptable duration between compromise detection and restored operational capacity is fifteen minutes for software-only deployments and four hours for DITL hardware deployments. The longer RTO for hardware reflects the physical replacement time for compromised coprocessors, including secure transport, physical installation, PUF re-enrollment, and constitutional schema re-anchoring. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Recovery Point Objective.** The RPO is designed to approach zero because the Immutable Ledger and blockchain anchors provide a complete, cryptographically verifiable record of every determination that occurred before the compromise event. The replacement infrastructure reconstructs its state from the ledger without losing any constitutional history. The exception is the three-hundred-second pre-anchoring window: logs in this window may be lost if the compromise destroys the local nvSRAM accumulator before Governance Lane anchoring completes. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Anchor Continuity Verification.** Before the replacement infrastructure begins issuing new determinations, it must verify that its reconstructed ledger state produces Merkle roots consistent with the most recent pre-compromise blockchain anchors. If inconsistency is detected, the infrastructure enters constitutional continuity audit mode and cannot issue Permission Tokens until the discrepancy is reconciled through external auditor review, chamber quorum validation, and public disclosure of the reconciliation methodology. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**DITL Chip Quarantine.** Newly fabricated DITL coprocessors replacing compromised hardware must undergo a thirty-day behavioral monitoring period before they are authorized to issue Permission Tokens. During quarantine, the chip operates in audit-only mode: evaluating proposals and generating Decision Logs but withholding Permission Tokens. This quarantine period extends the effective RTO for hardware recovery but reduces the risk of replacing a compromised chip with another compromised chip from the same fabrication batch. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Rollback Schema Validation.** When recovering from schema manipulation - where the compromise involved modifying the constitutional schema to introduce malicious parameters - the rollback target must be validated against a canonical schema version anchored to the Immutable Ledger before the compromise window. If no pre-compromise canonical version exists, the institution must adopt the most conservative available schema and re-approve all subsequent modifications through the full Tri-Cameral quorum process. This may be operationally disruptive, but the alternative - recovering onto a compromised schema - is constitutionally unacceptable. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)


## 10.10 The Closing Thesis: Hardware Resists Last. Institutions Fail First.

The adversarial survivability assessment produces a verdict that is simultaneously encouraging and sobering. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The encouraging finding: in full DITL hardware deployment, the framework achieves something that no prior governance architecture has achieved - physical non-bypassability of constitutional constraints. The electron does not negotiate. The C-element does not accept bribes. The memristive cell does not respond to political authority. For the first time in the history of economic governance, it is possible to construct a system whose core constraint - the requirement that execution be preceded by evidence - is enforced not by law, not by policy, not by institutional trust, but by physics.

The sobering finding: the path to full DITL hardware deployment is long, expensive, and subject to geopolitical disruption. No fabricated DITL chip meeting all six mandatory conditions currently exists. During the Transitional Emulation Mode that precedes hardware deployment, the framework's two most critical Pillars degrade to policy-only enforcement. The governance record remains intact. The execution gate does not. And the adversary who understands the framework will not wait for the hardware to be deployed. The adversary will attack the institutions that configure it, the appointment processes that populate its chambers, and the schema parameters that define its constitutional boundaries - using the ordinary tools of institutional capture that have defeated every prior governance framework.

Hardware resists last. Institutions fail first. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

This is not a concession of defeat. It is a specification of the adversarial priority order that institutions deploying TL must understand. The Tri-Cameral model's diversity requirements, supermajority thresholds, timelock mechanisms, pattern-of-drift penalties, and mandatory review protocols are not decorative. They are the institutional equivalent of the DITL hardware: the minimum specification for constitutional integrity in the domain where physics cannot reach. The adversary who captures an institution finds the hardware waiting. The adversary who captures the hardware finds the institution already compromised. The framework's resilience depends on neither failing before the other.

# SECTION 11: POST-QUANTUM CRYPTOGRAPHIC MIGRATION

## 11.0 Overview

The cryptographic infrastructure of Ternary Logic was designed to satisfy the security requirements of the present. The post-quantum migration protocol specified in this Section ensures that it continues to satisfy those requirements through the 2032 to 2040 vulnerability window and beyond. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The migration challenge is not merely technical. It is constitutional. The Immutable Ledger contains a complete historical record of every Decision Log, every Permission Token, and every governance determination since framework deployment. That record is anchored to public blockchains through ECDSA signatures. If quantum computers achieve sufficient capability to break ECDSA through Shor's algorithm, those historical anchors become forgeable. A regulator examining a ten-year-old governance record cannot verify that the record is authentic if the cryptographic signatures that authenticated it can be retroactively forged. The governance history of the framework - the entire evidentiary foundation on which its constitutional claims rest - becomes unreliable. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

This is not a future threat to future records. Harvest-now-decrypt-later attacks are already underway. Nation-state intelligence services are systematically collecting encrypted communications and blockchain signatures today, with the expectation that quantum computers will eventually enable retroactive forgery of any ECDSA-signed record collected before the migration. Every day that TL operates without the hybrid signature protocol is a day that its historical governance record accumulates quantum-vulnerable anchors.

Section 11 specifies the complete migration architecture: the algorithm selection rationale, the hybrid signature protocol that preserves Merkle chain continuity during the transition, the automatic trigger system that prevents institutional delay from creating dangerous exposure, the multi-chain anchoring redundancy during quantum transition, and the constitutional agility protocol that embeds post-quantum readiness into the framework's operational schema from initial deployment. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)


## 11.1 The Quantum Threat Landscape

Quantum computing threatens the mathematical foundations of public-key cryptography through two algorithms: Shor's algorithm for integer factorization and discrete logarithm problems, and Grover's algorithm for unstructured search. The threat profile of each differs substantially for TL's cryptographic infrastructure. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.1.1 Hash Function Resilience

SHA-256 and BLAKE3-256, the hash algorithms used for Merkle tree construction and Decision Log anchoring, retain post-quantum security against Grover's algorithm. A quantum computer running Grover's algorithm can search an unsorted database of size N in approximately the square root of N steps, reducing the effective security of a 256-bit hash from 256 bits to 128 bits. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The 128-bit quantum security margin is computationally infeasible under any optimistic estimate of near-term quantum computing progress. Even the most aggressive projections for fault-tolerant quantum computing do not place a 128-bit Grover search within the operational horizon of the next two decades. Doubling hash output lengths to SHA-512 or BLAKE3-512 would restore the full 256-bit quantum security margin, but this is not required for the current deployment horizon and would increase ledger storage requirements and Merkle proof sizes proportionally. The hash algorithms do not require immediate replacement. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.1.2 ECDSA Vulnerability

ECDSA, the elliptic curve digital signature algorithm used for Permission Token signatures, chamber authentication, and blockchain transaction signing, does not share this resilience. Shor's algorithm solves the discrete logarithm problem on which ECDSA security rests in polynomial time on a sufficiently large fault-tolerant quantum computer. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The security reduction is total, not partial. Whereas Grover's algorithm reduces hash security by a square root factor, Shor's algorithm reduces ECDSA security to zero once sufficient quantum hardware exists. An attacker with a cryptographically relevant quantum computer does not merely have an advantage over ECDSA verification - the attacker can derive the private signing key from any observed public key, forge arbitrary signatures on any message, and retroactively authenticate any historical record as if it had been signed by the legitimate private key holder. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

For TL's Immutable Ledger, this means that ECDSA-signed anchors on Bitcoin, Ethereum, and Polygon become forgeable. A state actor or well-funded adversary who has harvested the public keys from historical anchor transactions - which are permanently visible on all three chains - can retroactively produce signatures for any alternate transaction content, enabling the fabrication of a fraudulent governance history that cannot be distinguished from the authentic one through signature verification alone.

### 11.1.3 The Harvest-Now-Decrypt-Later Threat

The harvest-now-decrypt-later attack is already operationally active. Nation-state intelligence services with the resources and the motivation are collecting all publicly accessible ECDSA-signed data today - including blockchain transactions - with the expectation that sufficiently capable quantum hardware will become available within the decade. The collection cost is negligible. The storage cost is decreasing. The economic calculation favors collection now regardless of the uncertainty about quantum timeline. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

This means that the vulnerability window is not bounded by the date quantum computers become available. It is bounded by the date the hybrid signature protocol is activated. Every ECDSA anchor generated before hybrid activation is permanently quantum-vulnerable regardless of when quantum hardware actually arrives. An institution that delays hybrid activation by one year generates approximately thirty-one million seconds of additional quantum-vulnerable anchor accumulation. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The automatic trigger system specified in Section 11.4 addresses this by removing institutional discretion from the activation decision. The Stewardship Custodians configure threshold parameters that trigger hybrid activation automatically when quantum readiness indicators cross defined values, preventing the economic and operational pressures that would otherwise cause institutions to defer activation.

### 11.1.4 The Vulnerability Window: 2032 to 2040

The vulnerability window for ECDSA is estimated at 2032 to 2040. This estimate represents the period between the plausible emergence of cryptographically relevant quantum computers - defined as fault-tolerant systems with sufficient logical qubits and sufficiently low error rates to run Shor's algorithm against 256-bit elliptic curves - and the completion of global migration to post-quantum algorithms. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

NSA CNSA 2.0 sets 2030 as the mandatory migration deadline for National Security Systems - a deadline set deliberately in advance of the estimated vulnerability window to ensure completion before exposure. The UK National Cyber Security Centre has characterized post-quantum cryptography migration as a global-scale change to IT and operational technology systems, noting that hardware roots of trust implementing the NIST post-quantum standards were expected to become available during 2025. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The 2030 NSA deadline implies that TL deployments should initiate hybrid signature mode no later than 2028, providing a two-year buffer for full migration before the NSA's projected exposure onset. The automatic trigger system is designed to enforce this timeline regardless of institutional preference.


## 11.2 NIST Post-Quantum Algorithm Standards

NIST finalized three post-quantum cryptographic standards in August 2024. These standards represent the outcome of an eight-year international evaluation process that assessed over sixty candidate algorithms across three submission rounds for security strength, implementation efficiency, and resistance to both classical and quantum attacks. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.2.1 FIPS 203: ML-KEM-1024

FIPS 203 specifies Module-Lattice-Based Key-Encapsulation Mechanism, derived from the CRYSTALS-Kyber submission. ML-KEM-1024 is the highest security parameter set, providing security equivalent to AES-256 against both classical and quantum attacks. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

ML-KEM-1024 is used in TL for key encapsulation operations during the EKR ceremony: establishing the shared secret from which the ephemeral session key is derived. The module lattice security assumption means that breaking ML-KEM-1024 requires solving the Module Learning With Errors problem, for which no efficient quantum algorithm is known. The algorithm produces public keys of approximately 1568 bytes and ciphertexts of approximately 1568 bytes - larger than ECDH key exchanges but well within the bandwidth capacity of authenticated chamber communication channels. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.2.2 FIPS 204: ML-DSA (Dilithium)

FIPS 204 specifies Module-Lattice-Based Digital Signature Standard, derived from CRYSTALS-Dilithium. ML-DSA is the primary post-quantum digital signature standard and the direct replacement for ECDSA in TL's Permission Token signing, chamber authentication, and blockchain anchor transactions. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

ML-DSA at the highest security parameter set produces signatures of approximately 4627 bytes - significantly larger than the 64-byte ECDSA signature. This size increase has implications for ledger storage and blockchain transaction fees. The Merkle tree structure accommodates the larger signature sizes because each leaf hash is computed over the complete Decision Log including the full Dilithium signature, so the ledger's proof efficiency is independent of the signature size within the leaf. Blockchain anchor transactions carrying Dilithium signatures incur higher fees than ECDSA transactions, but the anchor frequency - one transaction per three-hundred-second Governance Lane cycle rather than per individual proposal - limits the fee impact to an operationally manageable level. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.2.3 FIPS 205: SLH-DSA-SHAKE-128s

FIPS 205 specifies Stateless Hash-Based Digital Signature Standard, derived from SPHINCS+. SLH-DSA provides a hash-based fallback signature option for deployments requiring long-term security without state management requirements. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Hash-based signatures derive their security from the collision resistance of the underlying hash function rather than from algebraic hardness assumptions. Their security is therefore reducible to SHA-256 or SHAKE-128 security, which retains the 128-bit quantum security margin described in Section 11.1.1. This makes SLH-DSA conservative by design: it makes fewer mathematical assumptions than ML-DSA and is more auditable because its security proof reduces to a single well-understood primitive.

SLH-DSA's primary operational limitation is signature size: the SHAKE-128s parameter set produces signatures of approximately 7856 bytes. In TL, SLH-DSA-SHAKE-128s is designated as the fallback for Stewardship Custodian chamber signatures in the highest-value governance operations where the conservative security proof justifies the storage overhead. It is not the default replacement for ECDSA in routine Permission Token operations. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The API Signature Block reserves slots for both ML-KEM-1024 and SLH-DSA-SHAKE-128s in addition to the primary ML-DSA slot, aligned with the NIST standards finalized in August 2024. These slots are present in the schema from initial deployment, ensuring forward compatibility without requiring a schema update at migration time.


## 11.3 The Hybrid Signature Protocol

The central technical challenge of post-quantum migration is preserving the Merkle chain continuity of the Immutable Ledger across the algorithm transition. A naive migration - replacing ECDSA signatures with Dilithium signatures on a specific cutover date - creates a ledger fork where pre-migration records are verifiable only with ECDSA and post-migration records are verifiable only with Dilithium. External auditors must maintain two verification stacks indefinitely. The cryptographic binding between pre-migration and post-migration records weakens. The constitutional chain of custody becomes ambiguous at the transition point. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The hybrid signature protocol resolves this by requiring that every Permission Token and chamber signature carry both an ECDSA signature and a Dilithium signature throughout the defined transition window.

### 11.3.1 Hybrid Leaf Structure

During the transition window, every Decision Log leaf in the Merkle tree carries a dual signature payload. The leaf hash is computed over the complete leaf content including both the ECDSA signature bytes and the Dilithium signature bytes. This creates a cryptographic link that is valid under either algorithm independently. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The Governance Lane verifies both signatures before issuing Proceed during the transition window. A Decision Proposal that carries a valid ECDSA signature but lacks a valid Dilithium signature receives Epistemic Hold: the evidentiary documentation is incomplete because the constitutional schema requires both signatures during the hybrid period. A proposal that carries a valid Dilithium signature but lacks a valid ECDSA signature similarly receives Epistemic Hold. Both signatures are required as long as the hybrid protocol is active.

This dual verification requirement is not a performance bottleneck in practice. ECDSA and Dilithium verification can proceed in parallel within the Governance Lane's evaluation pipeline. The total verification latency is bounded by the slower of the two operations, not their sum.

### 11.3.2 Merkle Chain Continuity

After the transition completes and the Stewardship Custodians vote through the supermajority process to retire ECDSA, the Merkle tree continues to incorporate the hybrid leaves from the transition period. External auditors can verify historical records using whichever algorithm they trust. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The dual-signature leaf structure means that neither algorithm can be retroactively removed without breaking the hash chain. A quantum attacker who derives the ECDSA private key from a historical public key and forges an alternate ECDSA signature cannot substitute this forged signature for the authentic one, because the Merkle leaf hash was computed over both signatures simultaneously. The forged ECDSA signature, computed over different leaf content than the original, produces a different hash. The hash chain breaks. The forgery is detected. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

This chain continuity guarantee is the core constitutional property of the hybrid protocol: historical governance records remain verifiable by auditors who trust only classical cryptography, by auditors who trust only post-quantum cryptography, and by auditors who require both. No single algorithm's compromise can retroactively corrupt the governance history.

### 11.3.3 Chamber Key Migration

The Tri-Cameral chambers hold the signing keys that authenticate every Permission Token. During the hybrid protocol, each chamber must maintain both its existing ECDSA key pair and its new Dilithium key pair simultaneously. The ECDSA key pairs are not immediately retired - they continue to sign every Token during the transition window in parallel with the new Dilithium signatures.

Key migration ceremonies for chamber signing keys follow the same physical presence and Shamir quorum requirements as other sensitive key operations. The new Dilithium key pairs are generated in hardware security modules under multi-party ceremony protocols. The enrollment of the new Dilithium public keys is anchored to the Immutable Ledger before the hybrid protocol is activated, so that the chain of custody for the post-quantum keys is itself verifiable from the moment of their introduction. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

ECDSA key retirement occurs through a Stewardship Custodian supermajority vote anchored to the Immutable Ledger after the Technical Council certifies that the Dilithium implementation has been validated against the NIST CAVP test vectors and that no operational dependency on ECDSA verification remains in any deployed system component. Retired ECDSA keys are cryptographically shredded through the standard HKDF-SHA3-256 destruction protocol used for all key lifecycle terminations.


## 11.4 Automatic Migration Triggers

The automatic trigger system prevents institutional delay from extending the quantum-vulnerable ECDSA-only exposure window beyond the constitutionally safe timeline. Unlike discretionary governance decisions that require Stewardship Custodian deliberation and supermajority approval, the migration trigger system activates automatically when quantitative threshold parameters embedded in the constitutional schema are crossed. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.4.1 Quantum Readiness Parameter

The Stewardship Custodians configure and maintain the Quantum Readiness Parameter - a composite score computed from four input streams.

**NIST Certification Stream.** The parameter tracks the status of NIST post-quantum algorithm standardization. When NIST finalizes a post-quantum digital signature standard suitable for TL's Permission Token signing use case, this stream advances the parameter score. NIST finalized FIPS 203, 204, and 205 in August 2024, advancing this stream to its maximum contribution.

**Academic Cryptanalysis Stream.** The parameter tracks peer-reviewed cryptanalysis of both the current ECDSA implementation and the candidate post-quantum algorithms. New attacks on ECDSA that reduce its effective security below defined thresholds advance the parameter score toward trigger activation. Successful cryptanalysis of a candidate post-quantum algorithm that reduces its security below acceptable levels would reduce that algorithm's suitability score and could require substitution with an alternative.

**Industry Deployment Stream.** The parameter tracks the commercial availability of hardware security modules that implement the selected post-quantum algorithms with FIPS 140-3 Level 3 certification. When HSMs with NIST-standardized post-quantum algorithm support become commercially available in quantities sufficient to support Tri-Cameral chamber key migration, this stream advances the score. The UK NCSC noted that hardware roots of trust implementing the NIST standards were expected to become available during 2025. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Intelligence Community Assessment Stream.** The parameter incorporates publicly available assessments from national cybersecurity agencies - CISA, NCSC, BSI, and equivalent bodies - regarding quantum computing progress and recommended migration timelines. When multiple agencies simultaneously advance their migration urgency recommendations, this stream contributes to parameter advancement.

### 11.4.2 Trigger Thresholds and Automatic Actions

**Threshold 1: Hybrid Protocol Activation.** When the Quantum Readiness Parameter crosses the first defined threshold, the Governance Lane automatically initiates the hybrid signature protocol. From this point forward, every Permission Token must carry both ECDSA and Dilithium signatures for Governance Lane acceptance. The Inference Lane's proposal generation pipeline receives automatic notification to begin including Dilithium signature capability in Decision Proposals. Chamber key migration ceremonies are scheduled by the Smart Contract Treasury's algorithmic agents. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Institutions that have not prepared their technical infrastructure for Dilithium signature generation begin receiving Epistemic Hold on all proposals from this point forward until their systems are updated. This creates a strong economic incentive for advance preparation: institutions that delay Dilithium implementation past Threshold 1 experience immediate operational disruption. The Smart Contract Treasury's fee schedule includes a transition preparation incentive that reduces governance fees for institutions that complete Dilithium readiness certification before Threshold 1 is crossed.

**Threshold 2: ECDSA Retirement Preparation.** When the Quantum Readiness Parameter crosses the second defined threshold - corresponding to conditions where independent security analysis indicates that ECDSA may be broken within a five-year horizon - the Governance Lane automatically initiates the ECDSA retirement preparation sequence. The Technical Council receives mandatory notification to begin validation of all system components' post-quantum-only operation capability. The Stewardship Custodians receive mandatory scheduling of ECDSA retirement vote. Blockchain anchor transactions begin generating single-use post-quantum accounts for the Ethereum and Polygon anchor channels. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Threshold 3: Full Post-Quantum Mode.** When the Stewardship Custodians complete the supermajority ECDSA retirement vote, the Governance Lane transitions to full Dilithium-only operation. ECDSA signature verification is removed from the five-layer NL=NA enforcement architecture. ECDSA signing capability is retired from all chamber HSMs through the standard key destruction protocol. Anchor transactions on all three blockchains transition to Dilithium-only signing. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The transition from Threshold 2 to Threshold 3 is the only step in the migration sequence that requires explicit Stewardship Custodian deliberation and supermajority vote. Thresholds 1 and 2 trigger automatically without requiring human authorization. This design ensures that even if the Stewardship Custodians face institutional pressure to delay migration, the hybrid protocol activates automatically and the transition preparation sequence begins regardless of institutional preferences.

### 11.4.3 Transition Window Management

The transition window - the period during which both ECDSA and Dilithium signatures are required simultaneously - should be long enough to ensure that all system components and counterparties have migrated to Dilithium capability, but short enough to minimize the period of dual-signature storage overhead and dual-verification processing. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The minimum transition window is twelve months: sufficient time for Technical Council validation of all deployed system components, Stewardship Custodian chamber key migration ceremonies, counterparty system updates, and regulatory notification in all applicable jurisdictions. The maximum transition window is thirty-six months, beyond which the dual-signature storage overhead becomes an operationally significant burden and the extended ECDSA retention increases the harvest-now-decrypt-later exposure window unnecessarily.

The exact transition window duration is configured by the Stewardship Custodians in the constitutional schema following Threshold 1 activation, subject to the twelve-to-thirty-six-month constitutional bounds. The chosen duration is anchored to the Immutable Ledger with the full Tri-Cameral signatures and becomes binding on all participants in the governance network.


## 11.5 Multi-Chain Anchoring During Quantum Transition

TL anchors Merkle roots to Bitcoin, Ethereum, and Polygon simultaneously. Each chain has different quantum vulnerability characteristics that affect the transition strategy for its anchor transactions. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.5.1 Bitcoin Anchor Considerations

Bitcoin's UTXO model provides some degree of natural quantum protection for unspent outputs: the public key is not revealed on the blockchain until an output is spent, so unspent outputs are protected against Shor's algorithm because there is no public key to apply the algorithm to. However, TL's anchor mechanism requires periodic transactions that expose the signing public key with every anchor publication. Each anchor transaction reveals the key for that anchor account, making it permanently quantum-vulnerable to harvest-now-decrypt-later collection. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Bitcoin does not yet support Dilithium signatures at the base protocol layer. The hybrid protocol handles Bitcoin anchors by maintaining dual-signature content in the OP_RETURN data payload of the anchor transaction, with the transaction itself signed under the existing ECDSA protocol. The Dilithium signature is embedded in the payload rather than in the transaction signature field. This preserves the Merkle chain's hybrid leaf structure for verifiability while accommodating Bitcoin's current signature protocol constraints. When Bitcoin protocol upgrades add native post-quantum signature support, the anchor transactions can migrate to native Dilithium signing.

### 11.5.2 Ethereum and Polygon Anchor Considerations

Ethereum and Polygon anchor transactions use single-use accounts: the signing private key is generated inside the DITL coprocessor's secure enclave and cryptographically shredded immediately after the transaction confirms. The public key is revealed by the transaction and is therefore permanently quantum-vulnerable to collection, but the destroyed private key means that an adversary who later derives the private key from the public key gains only the ability to spend the now-empty account. The anchor data and the Merkle root it records cannot be retroactively modified by possession of the private key. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Both Ethereum and Polygon support account abstraction mechanisms that enable Dilithium signature verification through smart contracts even before native protocol-level post-quantum support is added. TL's anchor contract is deployed at Threshold 1 activation to begin accepting Dilithium-signed anchor submissions alongside ECDSA-signed ones, enabling the hybrid anchor structure during the transition window.

### 11.5.3 Multi-Chain Redundancy During Transition

The specification mandates that a valid external anchor requires confirmation on at least two of the three chains during and after the quantum transition. If one chain experiences a quantum-related security incident - such as a successful Shor's attack against its signature scheme that enables reorganization of historical blocks - the other chains maintain the Merkle root record. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

If the quantum incident corrupts a chain's historical record by enabling retroactive block reorganization, the TL governance records anchored to that chain become unverifiable through that chain's history alone. The surviving chains continue to provide valid anchors, and the hybrid Merkle leaves include Dilithium signatures that are independently verifiable without reference to the compromised chain's ECDSA anchor. The redundancy ensures that no single chain's quantum failure destroys the governance record's verifiability.


## 11.6 The Constitutional Agility Protocol

Post-quantum migration is the most predictable major cryptographic transition TL will face. Future cryptographic developments may require additional migrations: advances in lattice cryptography that weaken ML-DSA, new algebraic attacks on hash functions that reduce effective security margins, or the development of new quantum algorithms that threaten primitives currently considered quantum-resistant. The constitutional agility protocol ensures that the framework can accommodate any required cryptographic transition without architectural disruption. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

### 11.6.1 Algorithm Slot Architecture

The TL API Signature Block is structured as a fixed-width header containing algorithm type identifiers alongside variable-width signature fields. Algorithm type identifiers are four-byte values drawn from a registry maintained by the Technical Council and anchored to the Immutable Ledger. The current registry includes slots for ECDSA-P256, ECDSA-P384, ML-DSA-87, SLH-DSA-SHAKE-128s, and ML-KEM-1024, as well as reserved slots for future algorithm additions. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

Adding a new algorithm to the registry does not require a schema update. It requires Technical Council certification of the algorithm's security properties against both classical and quantum attacks, Stewardship Custodian approval of the algorithm's inclusion in the registry through the standard schema modification process, and anchoring of the new registry entry to the Immutable Ledger. Once the registry entry is anchored, the algorithm is available for use in the next hybrid transition without any changes to the API schema's structural definition.

### 11.6.2 Retroactive Re-Anchoring

For historical records that were anchored using an algorithm that is later found to be broken, the constitutional agility protocol specifies a retroactive re-anchoring procedure. The Governance Lane generates a re-anchoring record: a new Merkle leaf containing the original leaf hash, the original signatures, and a new Dilithium signature computed over the concatenation of the original content and the re-anchoring timestamp. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The re-anchoring record is appended to the Immutable Ledger as a new leaf, not as a replacement for the original. The original record remains intact. The re-anchoring leaf creates a forward cryptographic link from the original content to the new post-quantum signature without modifying any historical record. External auditors verify both the original record and the re-anchoring leaf independently. The combination provides verification under both the original algorithm - available to auditors who have not yet transitioned their verification infrastructure - and the new algorithm - available to auditors who have. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The exact byte-level serialization of the re-anchoring record and the concatenation format for the new signature computation are specified at a high level in the Governance Complete source document and are tracked as near-term entries in the Constitutional Uncertainty Register pending Technical Council finalization of the encoding standard.


## 11.7 Institutional Preparation Requirements

The post-quantum migration places operational demands on institutions that deploy TL. These demands are not optional: they are constitutional obligations that are enforced through the automatic trigger system and the Smart Contract Treasury's penalty structure. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Hardware Security Module Upgrades.** Institutions must upgrade or replace HSMs that do not support ML-DSA and ML-KEM-1024 operations. The Technical Council maintains a certified HSM compatibility registry that lists approved modules. Institutions operating on non-certified HSMs receive automatic Epistemic Hold on all proposals at Threshold 1 activation. The Smart Contract Treasury's Recovery Reserve includes a hardware upgrade allocation that institutions can access through constitutional request, reducing but not eliminating the financial burden of the upgrade cycle.

**Capital Budgeting.** The ten-to-fifteen-year cryptographic horizon defines the planning window for institutional capital allocation. Organizations deploying TL must budget for the current ECDSA-based deployment and the post-quantum migration as sequential capital obligations. The Smart Contract Treasury is constitutionally required to allocate reserves for both migrations as obligations, not as discretionary IT projects. An institution that fails to budget for post-quantum migration will be unable to afford the transition when the Quantum Readiness Parameter crosses Threshold 1, forcing it either into constitutional non-compliance or into emergency borrowing that compromises its governance independence. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

**Counterparty Coordination.** Cross-border regulatory cooperation through the EKR mechanism requires that both the accessing party and the institution holding the records support compatible post-quantum signature verification. Institutions must coordinate with their principal regulatory counterparties and institutional partners to align migration timelines. The Stewardship Custodians maintain a counterparty readiness registry in the Regulatory Nexus that institutions can query to determine which of their counterparties have completed Dilithium readiness certification. Transactions with counterparties who have not completed certification at Threshold 2 activation receive Epistemic Hold pending counterparty migration confirmation.

**Regulatory Notification.** The constitutional schema modification that activates the hybrid protocol must be disclosed to all applicable financial supervisors as a material change to the institution's automated governance infrastructure. The Stewardship Custodians maintain jurisdiction-specific notification templates in the Regulatory Nexus that institutions can use to satisfy notification requirements. The notification Decision Log is anchored to the Immutable Ledger, creating a permanent record of regulatory disclosure compliance.


## 11.8 Tri-Cameral Oversight of Migration

The post-quantum migration is the largest coordinated cryptographic operation in the framework's lifecycle. Each chamber holds specific migration responsibilities that are constitutional obligations, not optional governance functions. [[6]](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/FractonicMind/TernaryLogic/refs/heads/main/Adversarial_Survivability/TL_Constitutional_Survivability_Under_Adversarial_Pressure.md)

The **Technical Council** monitors the Quantum Readiness Parameter inputs, evaluates post-quantum algorithm candidates against the security requirements of TL's specific use cases, validates HSM implementations against NIST CAVP test vectors, certifies the hybrid Merkle leaf structure for correctness and chain continuity, and manages the algorithm slot registry.
